This class is fairly specific to the needs of the producer. In\n * particular it has the following properties:\n * <ol>\n * <li>There is a special \"poolable size\" and buffers of this size are kept in a free list and recycled\n * <li>It is fair. That is all memory is given to the longest waiting thread until it has sufficient memory. This\n * prevents starvation or deadlock when a thread asks for a large chunk of memory and needs to block until multiple\n * buffers are deallocated.\n * </ol>\n */\npublic class BufferPool {\n\n deallocating\n     * @param metrics instance of Metrics\n     * @param time time instance\n     * @param metricGrpName logical group name for metrics\n     */\n    public BufferPool(long memory, int poolableSize, Metrics metrics, Time time, String metricGrpName) {\n        this.poolableSize = poolableSize;\n        this.lock = new ReentrantLock();\n        this.free = new ArrayDeque<>();\n        this.waiters = new ArrayDeque<>();\n        this.totalMemory = memory;\n        this.nonPooledAvailableMemory = memory;\n        this.metrics = metrics;\n        this.time = time;\n        this.waitTime = this.metrics.sensor(WAIT_TIME_SENSOR_NAME);\n        MetricName rateMetricName = metrics.metricName(\"bufferpool-wait-ratio\",\n                                                   metricGrpName,\n                                                   \"The fraction of time an appender waits for space allocation.\");\n        MetricName totalNsMetricName = nanoseconds an appender waits for space allocation.\");\n\n        Sensor bufferExhaustedRecordSensor = metrics.sensor(\"buffer-exhausted-records\");\n        MetricName bufferExhaustedRateMetricName bufferExhaustedTotalMetricName = metrics.metricName(\"buffer-exhausted-total\", metricGrpName, \"The total number of record sends that are dropped due to buffer exhaustion\");\n This method blocks if there is not enough memory and the buffer pool\n     * is configured with blocking mode.\n     *\n     * @param size The buffer size to allocate in bytes\n     * @param maxTimeToBlockMs The maximum time in milliseconds to block for buffer memory to be available\n     * @return The buffer\n     * @throws InterruptedException If the thread is interrupted while blocked\n     * @throws IllegalArgumentException if size is larger than the total memory controlled by the pool (and hence we would block\n     *         forever)\n     */\n    public ByteBuffer allocate(int size, long maxTimeToBlockMs) throws InterruptedException {\n        if (size > this.totalMemory)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Attempt to allocate \" + size\n                                               + \" bytes, but there is a hard limit of \"\n                                               + this.totalMemory\n                                               + \" on memory allocations.\");\n\n        ByteBuffer buffer = null;\n        this.lock.lock();\n\n        if (this.closed) {\n            this.lock.unlock();\n            throw new KafkaException(\"Producer closed while allocating memory\");\n        }\n\n        try {\n            // check if we have a free buffer of the right size pooled\n            if (size == poolableSize && !this.free.isEmpty())\n                return this.free.pollFirst();\n\n            // now check if the request is immediately satisfiable with the\n            // memory on hand or if we need to block\n            int freeListSize = freeSize() * this.poolableSize;\n            if (this.nonPooledAvailableMemory + freeListSize >= size) {\n                // we have enough unallocated or pooled memory to immediately\n                // satisfy the request, but need to allocate the buffer\n                freeUp(size);\n                this.nonPooledAvailableMemory -= size;\n            } else {\n                // we are out of memory and will have to block\n                int accumulated = 0;\n                Condition moreMemory = this.lock.newCondition();\n                try {\n                    long remainingTimeToBlockNs = TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS.toNanos(maxTimeToBlockMs);\n                    this.waiters.addLast(moreMemory);\n                    // loop over and over until we have a buffer or have reserved\n                    // enough memory to allocate one\n                    while (accumulated < size) {\n                        long startWaitNs = time.nanoseconds();\n                        long timeNs;\n                        boolean waitingTimeElapsed;\n                        try {\n                            waitingTimeElapsed = !moreMemory.await(remainingTimeToBlockNs, TimeUnit.NANOSECONDS);\n                        } finally {\n                            long endWaitNs = time.nanoseconds();\n                            timeNs = Math.max(0L, endWaitNs - startWaitNs);\n                            recordWaitTime(timeNs);\n                        }\n\n                        if (this.closed)\n                            throw new KafkaException(\"Producer closed while allocating memory\");\n\n                        if (waitingTimeElapsed) {\n                            this.metrics.sensor(\"buffer-exhausted-records\").record();\n                            throw new BufferExhaustedException(\"Failed to allocate \" + size + \" bytes within the configured max blocking time \"\n                                + maxTimeToBlockMs + \" ms. Total memory: \" + totalMemory() + \" bytes. Available memory: \" + availableMemory()\n                                + \" bytes. Poolable size: \" + poolableSize() + \" bytes\");\n                        }\n\n                        remainingTimeToBlockNs -= timeNs;\n\n                        // check if we can satisfy this request from the free list,\n                        // otherwise allocate memory\n                        if (accumulated == 0 && size == this.poolableSize && !this.free.isEmpty()) {\n                            // just grab a buffer from the free list\n                            buffer = this.free.pollFirst();\n                            accumulated = size;\n                        } else {\n                            // we'll need to allocate memory, but we may only get\n                            // part of what we need on this iteration\n                            freeUp(size - accumulated);\n                            int got = (int) Math.min(size - accumulated, this.nonPooledAvailableMemory);\n                            this.nonPooledAvailableMemory -= got;\n                            accumulated += got;\n                        }\n                    }\n                    // Don't reclaim memory on throwable since nothing was thrown\n                    accumulated = 0;\n                } finally {\n                    // When this loop was not able to successfully terminate don't loose available memory\n                    this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += accumulated;\n                    this.waiters.remove(moreMemory);\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            // signal any additional waiters if there is more memory left\n            // over for them\n            try {\n                if (!(this.nonPooledAvailableMemory == 0 && this.free.isEmpty()) && !this.waiters.isEmpty())\n                    this.waiters.peekFirst().signal();\n            } finally {\n                // Another finally... otherwise find bugs complains\n                lock.unlock();\n            }\n        }\n\n        if (buffer == null)\n            return safeAllocateByteBuffer(size);\n        else\n            return buffer;\n    }\n\n    // Protected for testing\n    protected void recordWaitTime(long timeNs) {\n        this.waitTime.record(timeNs, time.milliseconds());\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Allocate a buffer.  If buffer allocation fails (e.g. because of OOM) then return the size count back to\n     * available memory and signal the next waiter if it exists.\n     */\n    private ByteBuffer safeAllocateByteBuffer(int size) {\n        boolean error = true;\n        try {\n            ByteBuffer buffer = allocateByteBuffer(size);\n            error = false;\n            return buffer;\n        } finally {\n            if (error) {\n                this.lock.lock();\n                try {\n                    this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += size;\n                    if (!this.waiters.isEmpty())\n                        this.waiters.peekFirst().signal();\n                } finally {\n                    this.lock.unlock();\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Protected for testing.\n    protected ByteBuffer allocateByteBuffer(int size) {\n        return ByteBuffer.allocate(size);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Attempt to ensure we have at least the requested number of bytes of memory for allocation by deallocating pooled\n     * buffers (if needed)\n     */\n    private void freeUp(int size) {\n        while (!this.free.isEmpty() && this.nonPooledAvailableMemory < size)\n            this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += this.free.pollLast().capacity();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Return buffers to the pool. If they are of the poolable size add them to the free list, otherwise just mark the\n     * memory as free.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The buffer to return\n     * @param size The size of the buffer to mark as deallocated, note that this may be smaller than buffer.capacity\n     *             since the buffer may re-allocate itself during in-place compression\n     */\n    public void deallocate(ByteBuffer buffer, int size) {\n        lock.lock();\n        try {\n            if (size == this.poolableSize && size == buffer.capacity()) {\n                buffer.clear();\n                this.free.add(buffer);\n            } else {\n                this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += size;\n            }\n            Condition moreMem = this.waiters.peekFirst();\n            if (moreMem != null)\n                moreMem.signal();\n        } finally {\n            lock.unlock();\n        }\n    }\n\n    public void deallocate(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        if (buffer != null)\n            deallocate(buffer, buffer.capacity());\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * the total free memory both unallocated and in the free list\n     */\n    public long availableMemory() {\n        lock.lock();\n        try {\n            return this.nonPooledAvailableMemory + freeSize() * (long) this.poolableSize;\n        } finally {\n            lock.unlock();\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Protected for testing.\n    protected int freeSize() {\n        return this.free.size();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Get the unallocated memory (not in the free list or in use)\n     */\n    public long unallocatedMemory() {\n        lock.lock();\n        try {\n            return this.nonPooledAvailableMemory;\n        } finally {\n            lock.unlock();\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * The number of threads blocked waiting on memory\n     */\n    public int queued() {\n        lock.lock();\n        try {\n            return this.waiters.size();\n        } finally {\n            lock.unlock();\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * The buffer size that will be retained in the free list after use\n     */\n    public int poolableSize() {\n        return this.poolableSize;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * The total memory managed by this pool\n     */\n    public long totalMemory() {\n        return this.totalMemory;\n    }\n\n    // package-private method used only for testing\n I see something critical here at line 925-926:```java\nbatch.close();\nsize += batch.records().sizeInBytes();```\n\nThe batch is CLOSED before its records are accessed!Looking at ProducerBatch.close(), let me check what it does.\n\nFrom the ProducerBatch code I read earlier:```java\npublic void close() {\n    recordsBuilder.close();\n    if (!recordsBuilder.isControlBatch()) {\n        CompressionRatioEstimator.updateEstimation(topicPartition.topic(),\n                                                   recordsBuilder.compression().type(),\n                                                   (float) recordsBuilder.compressionRatio());\n    }\n    reopened = false;\n}\n```\n\nAnd closeForRecordAppends():```java\npublic void closeForRecordAppends() {\n    recordsBuilder.closeForRecordAppends();\n}\n```\n\nSo when the batch is closed, the recordsBuilder is closed. But the MemoryRecordsBuilder might still hold a reference to the buffer.Actually, looking back at line 926, batch.records() is called AFTER batch.close(). This builds the MemoryRecords from the buffer.Now, in sendProducerData, at line 395-396:```java\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n```\n\nAnd later at line 442:```java\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n```\n\nIn sendProduceRequests, at line 874:```java\nMemoryRecords records = batch.records();\n```\n\nAnd then at line 884-886, this MemoryRecords is added to the request:```java\ntpData.partitionData().add(new ProduceRequestData.PartitionProduceData()\n        .setIndex(tp.partition())\n        .setRecords(records));\n```\n\nSo the MemoryRecords is held in the ProduceRequestData. The request is then constructed at line 897-903 with the topicData containing these records, and sent via the client at line 912-913.\n\nThe requestBuilder is passed to newClientRequest, but serialization doesn't happen immediately—it occurs when the request is actually transmitted over the network. This creates a potential race condition: the batches get drained and added to inflight, the request is built with batch.records(), sent to the client without yet being serialized, and then the batch expires and deallocates, returning the buffer to the pool. A new batch could reuse that buffer, and when the network client finally serializes the request, it reads from corrupted memory.\n\nThe critical window is between when a batch is drained and added to inflight versus when sendProduceRequest is invoked. Looking at the sequence: batches drain at line 395, get added to inflight at 396, expired inflight batches are collected at 406-407, and those are failed and deallocated at 415-423. Only after all this does sendProduceRequests execute at line 442. If a batch expires during this window—after being drained but before the request is sent—the buffer gets freed while still referenced by the unserialized request.\n\nFor this to happen, the batch would need to exceed its delivery timeout immediately after draining. Since expiration checks if `deliveryTimeoutMs <= now - createdMs`, a batch created long ago could theoretically expire right after being drained if enough time has passed.\n\nThe key issue is that `createdMs` isn't updated when a batch is drained—it reflects when the batch was first added to the accumulator. So a batch lingering in the accumulator for an extended period (due to `linger.ms` or other delays) could age enough to trigger expiration while simultaneously being processed in the drain and send flow.\n\nLooking at the expiration logic in `getExpiredInflightBatches`, batches are expected to be in-flight and not yet completed. The critical sequence occurs when: a batch gets drained and moved to inflight, then before it's actually sent, enough time elapses that it appears in the expired list, gets removed from inflight, and gets failed—all while the same batch might still be getting processed downstream.\n\nThe race condition emerges because `sendProduceRequests` at line 442 operates on a batches map that could contain a batch whose buffer was already deallocated during the expiration check. This happens if the batch expires between being added to inflight and being sent, particularly when `delivery.timeout.ms` is configured with a short duration or there's latency between the drain operation and the expiration check.\n\nBut there's another angle here—broker disconnections could trigger deallocation independently of timeout expiration. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Dqxibrk6QSxegB9tGNfEv9","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the key issue! Look at the flow:\n\nIn sendProducerData():1. Line 395: batches are drained from the accumulator\n2. Line 396: batches are added to inflight\n3. Line 442: sendProduceRequests(batches, now) is called\n\nIn sendProduceRequest():1. Line 874: batch.records() is called to get MemoryRecords\n2. The request is built with this MemoryRecords\n3. Line 909: A callback is set up: `RequestCompletionHandler callback = response -> handleProduceResponse(response, recordsByPartition, topicNames, time.milliseconds());`\n4. Line 914: client.send(clientRequest, now) is called\n\nThe critical issue is:- The MemoryRecords is built from batch.records() at line 874\n- But the SERIALIZATION of the request (including the MemoryRecords) happens LATER when the network layer actually sends the bytes\n- If the batch expires AFTER the request is built but BEFORE it's serialized, the buffer will be deallocated and reused\n- When the network layer tries to serialize the request, it will read corrupted data from the reused buffer\n\nNow, the question is: when can a batch expire between lines 395 and 914?\n\nLooking at the code:- Line 395-396: Batch is drained and added to inflight\n- Line 406-423: Expired batches are checked and deallocated\n- But at this point, the batch is a PREVIOUSLY in-flight batch, not one that was just drained\n\nUnless... wait, I think I see the real issue now!\n\nLooking at the handleProduceResponse callback at line 909:```java\nRequestCompletionHandler callback = response -> handleProduceResponse(response, recordsByPartition, topicNames, time.milliseconds());\n```\n\nThis is a callback that captures `recordsByPartition` and `topicNames`. The `recordsByPartition` map contains the mapping from TopicPartition to the batch.\n\n\nThe callback executes asynchronously when the response arrives, and in handleProduceResponse at line 618, the batch is retrieved and then completed at line 623, which triggers maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch. The real problem might be that the batch could expire while the request is still in flight—between when it's built and when it's actually serialized by the network layer. If expiration happens during serialization, the buffer gets deallocated while the network code is still reading from it. The Sender thread is supposed to be single-threaded, so concurrent access shouldn't occur. But I realize the requestBuilder might not be serialized immediately—it's lazily built when the network client actually needs to transmit it. When batch.records() is called, it invokes MemoryRecordsBuilder.build() to construct the MemoryRecords from the underlying buffer. These records are then wrapped into the ProduceRequestData, which gets passed along for eventual network transmission.\n\nThe critical issue is that ProduceRequestData holds a reference to the MemoryRecords and its ByteBuffer, but the actual serialization to bytes doesn't happen until the network layer sends the request. This creates a window where the buffer could be reused or modified before serialization completes.\n\nThe race condition unfolds like this: after the batch is drained and its records wrapped in MemoryRecords, the request gets queued for network transmission. Meanwhile, if the batch expires during this window, its buffer gets returned to the pool and reallocated for new data. When the network client finally attempts to serialize the ProduceRequestData, it reads from a corrupted or reused buffer instead of the original batch data.\n\nThe specific vulnerability occurs when a batch becomes ready to send but is simultaneously old enough to trigger expiration—the topic name and other metadata get overwritten as the buffer cycles through the pool. The sendProduceRequest method retrieves TopicProduceData by topic name at line 876, but if that underlying buffer has been corrupted by reuse, the serialization produces requests with scrambled topic assignments. The produce request header is serialized separately from the message payload, so corruption there would cause messages to route to the wrong topic. This could happen if the request header references a buffer that gets deallocated and reused, or if serialization reads from an incorrect buffer location. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Xz1U7CqBXnuBb1FV9h3NXm","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Great! I found the key part. Looking at line 74 and 83-89:\n```java\n// In writeTo method:\nreturn Utils.tryWriteTo(channel, position, length, buffer);\n\n// In writeFullyTo method:\nwhile (written < sizeInBytes())\n    written += channel.write(buffer);\n```\n\nSo MemoryRecords holds a reference to the ByteBuffer and writes directly from it when sending data! This is the exact scenario where the race condition occurs:\n\n1. batch.records() is called at line 874 in sendProduceRequest, which creates a MemoryRecords wrapping the ByteBuffer\n2. The MemoryRecords is stored in ProduceRequestData\n3. The request is sent to the network client\n4. When the network layer actually sends the data (in writeFullyTo or writeTo), it reads directly from the buffer\n5. If the batch has expired and its buffer was deallocated and reused, the data being sent comes from the wrong buffer!\n\nNow, the remaining question is: can a batch that was just drained become expired before its request is fully sent?\n\nLooking at the sendProducerData flow:\n- Line 395-396: Batch is drained and added to inflight\n- Line 406-423: Expired batches are checked and deallocated\n- Line 442: sendProduceRequests is called, which eventually sends the request asynchronously\n\nThe request sending might not be synchronous! Let me check when the actual network sending happens.Actually, looking at line 914 in sendProduceRequest:\n```java\nclient.send(clientRequest, now);\n```\n\nThis sends the request to the KafkaClient. The KafkaClient probably queues the request and sends it later when the socket is ready.\n\nSo the race condition is:\n1. Batch A is drained and added to inflight\n2. sendProduceRequests(batches) is called\n3. For Batch A, batch.records() is called, creating a MemoryRecords\n\n\n4. The request is queued in the client but not yet transmitted\n5. Before the socket actually writes the data, Batch A expires and its buffer gets deallocated and reused for Batch B\n6. When the client finally flushes the request to the network, it reads from the reallocated buffer containing Batch B's data instead\n\nThis could happen if Batch A was created long ago with a high linger.ms value but only became ready to send due to some other condition like reaching batch size or a force flush, meaning its creation timestamp is old enough to trigger expiration checks before transmission completes.\n\nHowever, looking at the actual flow in sendProducerData, expired batches are identified and failed at line 406-407, which happens before sendProduceRequests is invoked at line 415-423. So a batch that's both drained and expired would be caught and failed before it ever reaches the client for sending.\n\nThe real issue must involve batches already in flight from previous calls. When a batch that was sent in an earlier sendProducerData invocation times out waiting for a broker response, failBatch deallocates its buffer. But the network layer might still be actively transmitting that request, reading from the now-freed buffer and getting corrupted data from whatever reused that memory.\n\nThe serialization of the request happens asynchronously after the batch is added to inflight, so if the buffer gets deallocated before the write completes, the network layer reads from the wrong memory. The solution would involve either deferring buffer deallocation until transmission finishes, copying the data before freeing it, or preventing buffer reuse while requests are still being sent. I need to trace where the actual request serialization occurs and when the buffer gets accessed during that process.\n\nLooking at the code flow, when `sendProduceRequest()` builds the request using `batch.records()`, the MemoryRecords reference is embedded in the ProduceRequestData. The actual serialization happens later in the network layer, but if the batch expires and its buffer is deallocated between request creation and serialization completion, the write operation accesses freed or reused memory. The callback handler at line 909 suggests there's a completion mechanism that could be leveraged to defer cleanup until after the request is fully transmitted.\n\nExamining the `sendProducerData()` method more carefully, I notice batches are drained at line 395 and added to inflight at line 396, but then expired batches are retrieved at line 406 and deallocated before `sendProduceRequests()` even completes. This means the buffer could be freed while the request is still being serialized in the network layer. failed before being sent. A batch can be drained from the accumulator at line 395, added to the inflight list, and then discovered as expired at line 407 within the same call. When failBatch deallocates it at line 418, the batch is still referenced in the batches list that sendProduceRequests will iterate over, causing it to access freed memory when calling batch.records().\n\nThe key insight is that drained batches—those ready to send based on linger.ms and batch size—can be quite old and simultaneously exceed the delivery timeout threshold. This means a single batch can be both in the ready list and the expired list, creating the race condition where it gets deallocated before sendProduceRequest tries to use But Batch A is still in the batches map from step 2!\n6. sendProduceRequests(batches) is called at line 442, which tries to access Batch A's records\n\nThe race condition is that a batch can be drained and added to the inflight map, then immediately expired and deallocated, all within the same sendProducerData call. This leaves a reference to the deallocated batch in the batches collection that gets passed to sendProduceRequests.\n\nThe key insight is that when a batch is retried after a failure, reenqueueBatch() preserves its original createdMs timestamp. This means a batch that was created long ago, failed, and is being retried could be old enough to expire immediately upon the next drain cycle. The batch gets drained because it's ready to send, but then expires before sendProduceRequests can safely access its records, causing the use-after-free. the batch, but its buffer has been deallocated!\n\nThis is the race condition. The fix would be to check expiration before draining, or avoid deallocating batches immediately after they're drained. Looking at the drain flow in drainBatchesForOneNode around line 862, there's a backoff check before draining, and at line 889 there's a condition to stop draining for a partition. These checks might not account for the expiration timing issue between when a batch is drained and when it's removed from inflight.\n\nI need to examine what shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition actually does to understand if it's catching this race Alternatively, if the batch is marked as done via isDone() before sendProduceRequest accesses it, that would prevent the issue. In failBatch(), calling batch.completeExceptionally() sets the batch to FAILED state and marks it as done, so when sendProduceRequest tries to access the batch's records, the records() method still builds from the recordsBuilder without checking if the batch is done. This means even a completed batch can attempt to build from a deallocated buffer. The actual issue stems from how batches are drained from the accumulator at line 395—they're not yet in inflight at that point. Then at line 396, they get added to inflight, but if deallocation happens before sendProduceRequests runs, the buffer is already freed when the request tries to access it.\n\nThe problem is that getExpiredInflightBatches() can mark batches as expired in the same call where they were just added to inflight. A better approach would be to validate expiration before adding batches to inflight, or prevent deallocation of batches within the same sendProducerData call that added them. Looking at line 442 where sendProduceRequests is invoked with the batches map, that map still contains references that could have been deallocated by the expiration {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01FifEP37BLT8iUGehRw5NqG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_0152LuwtcjZ2xnRrnWjsabCf","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition - Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer sending logic, contains `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Batch representation, manages MemoryRecordsBuilder and buffer lifecycle\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Accumulates records and manages batch draining/deallocation\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory pool for ByteBuffer reuse with lock-based allocation/deallocation\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/MemoryRecords.java` — Holds direct reference to ByteBuffer, reads from it during `writeTo()` and `writeFullyTo()` calls\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `Sender.sendProduceRequest()` (line 874)\n   - Calls `batch.records()` to get MemoryRecords wrapping the ByteBuffer\n   - MemoryRecords is stored in ProduceRequestData and sent to network layer\n\n2. **Called from**: `Sender.sendProduceRequests()` (line 856)\n   - Iterates through drained batches and calls `sendProduceRequest()` for each\n\n3. **Batch added to inflight at**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 396)\n   - `addToInflightBatches(batches)` adds newly drained batches to the inFlightBatches map\n\n4. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-418)\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` removes expired batches from inFlightBatches list\n   - `failBatch()` calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`\n   - Buffer is returned to BufferPool and can be immediately reused by other threads\n\n5. **Race condition window**: Between line 418 and 442 in `Sender.sendProducerData()`\n   - Batch is deallocated before `sendProduceRequests(batches)` is called\n   - Batch is still in the `batches` map and will be sent\n   - MemoryRecords holds stale reference to deallocated buffer\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Functions**: `sendProducerData()` (line 357-443) and `failBatch()` (line 817-837)\n\n**Line**: ~406-442 (race condition window)\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe race condition occurs due to the following sequence in `sendProducerData()`:\n\n```java\n// Line 395-396: Drain batches and add to inflight\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n\n// Line 406-407: Get expired batches (including those just added to inflight!)\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\nexpiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n\n// Line 415-423: Deallocate expired batches\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false);  // Line 418\n    // This calls maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() → accumulator.deallocate() → BufferPool.deallocate()\n}\n\n// Line 442: STILL tries to send the deallocated batches!\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n```\n\n**The core issue**:\n\n1. **Batch can be drained yet expired**: When a batch sits in the accumulator for a long time (due to large `linger.ms` or queuing), its `createdMs` timestamp becomes old. Even though the batch is just now \"ready\" to drain, it may exceed the `delivery.timeout.ms` threshold and be considered expired.\n\n2. **Expiration check includes newly drained batches**: The `getExpiredInflightBatches()` method iterates through `inFlightBatches` map, which now includes batches added at line 396. A batch drained at line 395 can also be expired at line 406 if:\n   - `now - batch.createdMs >= accumulator.getDeliveryTimeoutMs()`\n\n3. **Batch deallocated before sending**: When `failBatch()` is called at line 418, it invokes `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` which calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)` → `BufferPool.deallocate(buffer)`. The buffer is immediately returned to the pool and can be reused.\n\n4. **MemoryRecords holds stale buffer reference**: The `batch.records()` call at line 874 in `sendProduceRequest()` returns a `MemoryRecords` object that wraps the ByteBuffer. When this request is eventually serialized by the network layer (via `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` at line 74 or `writeFullyTo()` at line 83-89), it reads directly from the now-reused buffer.\n\n5. **Silent data corruption**: Since the buffer has been reused for a different batch (e.g., for topic B), the serialization reads garbage data. The CRC checksum in records passes because it only covers key/value/headers, not the produce request header. The corrupted produce request header (containing topic/partition) is sent to the broker, causing messages to appear on the wrong topic.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to **prevent deallocating a batch before its request is sent**, or **remove deallocated batches from the send queue**. The cleanest solution is to remove expired batches from the batches map before deallocating them:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -415,6 +415,7 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n             log.trace(\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\", expiredBatches.size());\n         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n+            batches.values().forEach(list -> list.remove(expiredBatch));\n             String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n                 + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n```\n\n**Alternative (more robust) fix**: Remove the batch from inflight BEFORE deallocating, and add a guard check in `sendProduceRequests()`:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -869,6 +869,12 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection tpd = new ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection();\n         for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n             TopicPartition tp = batch.topicPartition;\n+\n+            // Skip batches that have already been deallocated (expired before sending)\n+            if (batch.isDone() && batch.finalState() == ProducerBatch.FinalState.FAILED) {\n+                continue;\n+            }\n+\n             MemoryRecords records = batch.records();\n             Uuid topicId = topicIds.get(tp.topic());\n             ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceData tpData = tpd.find(tp.topic(), topicId);\n```\n\nThe **first fix is preferred** because it's simpler and prevents the batch from ever being sent if it's already failed.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Producer sends messages to topic A** at various times with `linger.ms` configured\n2. **Batch waits in accumulator** for either batch size threshold or linger time\n3. **Batch becomes ready and is drained** from accumulator into `batches` map in `sendProducerData()` at line 395\n4. **Batch is added to inFlightBatches** at line 396, marking it as \"in flight\"\n5. **Expiration check runs** at line 406, iterating through inFlightBatches\n6. **Batch is found expired** because `createdMs` is old (timestamp from initial creation) but `now` has exceeded `delivery.timeout.ms`\n7. **Batch is removed from inFlightBatches** during iteration at line 191 in `getExpiredInflightBatches()`\n8. **failBatch() is called** at line 418, which calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `accumulator.deallocate()`\n9. **Buffer is released to BufferPool** and immediately becomes available for reuse\n10. **New batch for topic B** (from another thread or subsequent sends) allocates the reused buffer\n11. **sendProduceRequests() is still called** at line 442 with the original `batches` map containing the now-deallocated batch\n12. **batch.records() creates MemoryRecords** wrapping the deallocated buffer at line 874\n13. **Request is built with corrupted MemoryRecords** and queued for sending\n14. **Network layer serializes request** by calling `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` which reads from the reused buffer\n15. **Buffer now contains topic B's data**, so serialization includes wrong topic information\n16. **Broker receives request** with topic A's partition but topic B's data\n17. **Messages appear on topic B** while being sent to topic A's partition\n\n### Why This Is a Race Condition\n\nThe race condition is NOT between multiple threads (the Sender is single-threaded), but rather a **timing race between expiration checking and request sending within the same single-threaded method**.\n\nThe vulnerability exists because:\n- No check prevents a batch from being both drained AND expired in the same `sendProducerData()` call\n- No synchronization between deallocating a batch and sending its buffered request\n- The `batches` map is not cleared of deallocated batches before `sendProduceRequests()` is called\n- MemoryRecords holds a direct reference to the ByteBuffer without copying data\n\n### When This Manifests\n\n- When `delivery.timeout.ms` is relatively small\n- When `linger.ms` is large, causing batches to accumulate and age\n- During broker restarts/network disruptions (metrics show \"bursts\")\n- With high throughput where buffers are quickly reused\n- Most likely to occur when a batch is drained after being dequeued and retried multiple times\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2258,"cache_read_input_tokens":67913,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2258},"output_tokens":7,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4bb75ef4-45ce-4348-86cb-b5dfe5e32610","uuid":"686a228e-2fbb-4da8-bc00-e6ea46f5d64e"}

Iterates through drained batches and calls `sendProduceRequest()` for each\n\n3. **Batch added to inflight at**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 396)\n   - `addToInflightBatches(batches)` adds newly drained batches to the inFlightBatches map\n\n4. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-418)\n   - Batch is deallocated before `sendProduceRequests(batches)` is called\n   - Batch is still in the `batches` map and will be sent\n   - MemoryRecords holds stale reference to deallocated buffer\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Functions**: `sendProducerData()` (line 357-443) and `failBatch()` (line 817-837)\n\n**Line**: ~406-442 (race condition window)\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe race condition occurs due to the following sequence in `sendProducerData()`:\n\n```java\n// Line 395-396: Drain batches and add to inflight\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n\n// Line 406-407: Get expired batches (including those just added to inflight!)\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\nexpiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n\n// Line 415-423: Deallocate expired batches\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false);  // Line 418\n    // This calls maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() → accumulator.deallocate() → BufferPool.deallocate()\n}\n\n// Line 442: STILL tries to send the deallocated batches!\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n```\n\n**The core issue**:\n\n1. **Batch can be drained yet expired**: When a batch sits in the accumulator for a long time (due to large `linger.ms` or queuing), its `createdMs` timestamp becomes old. Even though the batch is just now \"ready\" to drain, it may exceed the `delivery.timeout.ms` threshold and be considered expired.\n\n2. **Expiration check includes newly drained batches**: The `getExpiredInflightBatches()` method iterates through `inFlightBatches` map, which now includes batches added at line 396. A batch drained at line 395 can also be expired at line 406 if:\n   - `now - batch.createdMs >= accumulator.getDeliveryTimeoutMs()`\n\n3. **Batch deallocated before sending**: When `failBatch()` is called at line 418, it invokes `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` which calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)` → `BufferPool.deallocate(buffer)`. The buffer is immediately returned to the pool and can be reused.\n\n4. **MemoryRecords holds stale buffer reference**: The `batch.records()` call at line 874 in `sendProduceRequest()` returns a `MemoryRecords` object that wraps the ByteBuffer. When this request is eventually serialized by the network layer (via `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` at line 74 or `writeFullyTo()` at line 83-89), it reads directly from the now-reused buffer.\n\n5. **Silent data corruption**: Since the buffer has been reused for a different batch (e.g., for topic B), the serialization reads garbage data. The CRC checksum in records passes because it only covers key/value/headers, not the produce request header. The corrupted produce request header (containing topic/partition) is sent to the broker, causing messages to appear on the wrong topic.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to **prevent deallocating a batch before its request is sent**, or **remove deallocated batches from the send queue**. The cleanest solution is to remove expired batches from the batches map before deallocating them:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -415,6 +415,7 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n             log.trace(\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\", expiredBatches.size());\n         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n+            batches.values().forEach(list -> list.remove(expiredBatch));\n             String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n                 + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n```\n\n**Alternative (more robust) fix**: Remove the batch from inflight BEFORE deallocating, and add a guard check in `sendProduceRequests()`:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -869,6 +869,12 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection tpd = new ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection();\n         for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n             TopicPartition tp = batch.topicPartition;\n+\n+            // Skip batches that have already been deallocated (expired before sending)\n+            if (batch.isDone() && batch.finalState() == ProducerBatch.FinalState.FAILED) {\n+                continue;\n+            }\n+\n             MemoryRecords records = batch.records();\n             Uuid topicId = topicIds.get(tp.topic());\n             ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceData tpData = tpd.find(tp.topic(), topicId);\n```\n\nThe **first fix is preferred** because it's simpler and prevents the batch from ever being sent if it's already failed.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Producer sends messages to topic A** at various times with `linger.ms` configured\n2. **Batch waits in accumulator** for either batch size threshold or linger time\n3. **Batch becomes ready and is drained** from accumulator into `batches` map in `sendProducerData()` at line 395\n4. **Batch is added to inFlightBatches** at line 396, marking it as \"in flight\"\n5. **Expiration check runs** at line 406, iterating through inFlightBatches\n6. **Batch is found expired** because `createdMs` is old (timestamp from initial creation) but `now` has exceeded `delivery.timeout.ms`\n7. **Batch is removed from inFlightBatches** during iteration at line 191 in `getExpiredInflightBatches()`\n8. **failBatch() is called** at line 418, which calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `accumulator.deallocate()`\n9. **Buffer is released to BufferPool** and immediately becomes available for reuse\n10. **New batch for topic B** (from another thread or subsequent sends) allocates the reused buffer\n11. **sendProduceRequests() is still called** at line 442 with the original `batches` map containing the now-deallocated batch\n12. **batch.records() creates MemoryRecords** wrapping the deallocated buffer at line 874\n13. **Request is built with corrupted MemoryRecords** and queued for sending\n14. **Network layer serializes request** by calling `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` which reads from the reused buffer\n15. **Buffer now contains topic B's data**, so serialization includes wrong topic information\n16. **Broker receives request** with topic A's partition but topic B's data\n17. **Messages appear on topic B** while being sent to topic A's partition\n\n### Why This Is a Race Condition\n\nThe race condition is NOT between multiple threads (the Sender is single-threaded), but rather a **timing race between expiration checking and request sending within the same single-threaded method**.\n\nThe vulnerability exists because:\n- No check prevents a batch from being both drained AND expired in the same `sendProducerData()` call\n- No synchronization between deallocating a batch and sending its buffered request\n- The `batches` map is not cleared of deallocated batches before `sendProduceRequests()` is called\n- MemoryRecords holds a direct reference to the ByteBuffer without copying data\n\n### When This Manifests\n\n- When `delivery.timeout.ms` is relatively small\n- When `linger.ms` is large, causing batches to accumulate and age\n- During broker restarts/network disruptions (metrics show \"bursts\")\n- With high throughput where buffers are quickly reused\n- Most likely to occur when a batch is drained after being dequeued and retried multiple times\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

The cleanest solution is to remove expired batches from the batches map before deallocating them:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -415,6 +415,7 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n             log.trace(\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\", expiredBatches.size());\n         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n+            batches.values().forEach(list -> list.remove(expiredBatch));\n             String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n                 + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n```\n\n**Why this fix works**:\n- The `batches` map is built from drained batches at line 395\n- If a batch is expired at line 406-407, it's added to `expiredBatches`\n- By removing it from `batches` before deallocating, we ensure `sendProduceRequests()` never attempts to send a deallocated batch\n- The batch still fails with the appropriate timeout exception, and users are notified\n- No request is sent with corrupted buffer data\n\n**Defensive alternative**: Add a guard in `sendProduceRequests()` to skip batches that are already done:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -869,6 +869,12 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection tpd = new ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection();\n         for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n             TopicPartition tp = batch.topicPartition;\n+\n+            // Skip batches that were already failed/completed (e.g., expired before sending)\n+            if (batch.isDone()) {\n+                continue;\n+            }\n+\n             MemoryRecords records = batch.records();\n             Uuid topicId = topicIds.get(tp.topic());\n             ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceData tpData = tpd.find(tp.topic(), topicId);\n```\n\n**Recommended approach**: Use the **first fix** (removing from batches map) as the primary solution, combined with the **defensive guard** as a safety measure. This provides defense-in-depth against the race condition.","originalFile":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition - Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer sending logic, contains `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Batch representation, manages MemoryRecordsBuilder and buffer lifecycle\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Accumulates records and manages batch draining/deallocation\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory pool for ByteBuffer reuse with lock-based allocation/deallocation\n- `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/MemoryRecords.java` — Holds direct reference to ByteBuffer, reads from it during `writeTo()` and `writeFullyTo()` calls\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `Sender.sendProduceRequest()` (line 874)\n   - Calls `batch.records()` to get MemoryRecords wrapping the ByteBuffer\n   - MemoryRecords is stored in ProduceRequestData and sent to network layer\n\n2. **Called from**: `Sender.sendProduceRequests()` (line 856)\n   - Iterates through drained batches and calls `sendProduceRequest()` for each\n\n3. **Batch added to inflight at**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 396)\n   - `addToInflightBatches(batches)` adds newly drained batches to the inFlightBatches map\n\n4. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-418)\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` removes expired batches from inFlightBatches list\n   - `failBatch()` calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`\n   - Buffer is returned to BufferPool and can be immediately reused by other threads\n\n5. **Race condition window**: Between line 418 and 442 in `Sender.sendProducerData()`\n   - Batch is deallocated before `sendProduceRequests(batches)` is called\n   - Batch is still in the `batches` map and will be sent\n   - MemoryRecords holds stale reference to deallocated buffer\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n**Functions**: `sendProducerData()` (line 357-443) and `failBatch()` (line 817-837)\n\n**Line**: ~406-442 (race condition window)\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe race condition occurs due to the following sequence in `sendProducerData()`:\n\n```java\n// Line 395-396: Drain batches and add to inflight\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n\n// Line 406-407: Get expired batches (including those just added to inflight!)\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\nexpiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n\n// Line 415-423: Deallocate expired batches\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false);  // Line 418\n    // This calls maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() → accumulator.deallocate() → BufferPool.deallocate()\n}\n\n// Line 442: STILL tries to send the deallocated batches!\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n```\n\n**The core issue**:\n\n1. **Batch can be drained yet expired**: When a batch sits in the accumulator for a long time (due to large `linger.ms` or queuing), its `createdMs` timestamp becomes old. Even though the batch is just now \"ready\" to drain, it may exceed the `delivery.timeout.ms` threshold and be considered expired.\n\n2. **Expiration check includes newly drained batches**: The `getExpiredInflightBatches()` method iterates through `inFlightBatches` map, which now includes batches added at line 396. A batch drained at line 395 can also be expired at line 406 if:\n   - `now - batch.createdMs >= accumulator.getDeliveryTimeoutMs()`\n\n3. **Batch deallocated before sending**: When `failBatch()` is called at line 418, it invokes `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` which calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)` → `BufferPool.deallocate(buffer)`. The buffer is immediately returned to the pool and can be reused.\n\n4. **MemoryRecords holds stale buffer reference**: The `batch.records()` call at line 874 in `sendProduceRequest()` returns a `MemoryRecords` object that wraps the ByteBuffer. When this request is eventually serialized by the network layer (via `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` at line 74 or `writeFullyTo()` at line 83-89), it reads directly from the now-reused buffer.\n\n5. **Silent data corruption**: Since the buffer has been reused for a different batch (e.g., for topic B), the serialization reads garbage data. The CRC checksum in records passes because it only covers key/value/headers, not the produce request header. The corrupted produce request header (containing topic/partition) is sent to the broker, causing messages to appear on the wrong topic.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to **prevent deallocating a batch before its request is sent**, or **remove deallocated batches from the send queue**. The cleanest solution is to remove expired batches from the batches map before deallocating them:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -415,6 +415,7 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n             log.trace(\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\", expiredBatches.size());\n         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n+            batches.values().forEach(list -> list.remove(expiredBatch));\n             String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n                 + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n```\n\n**Alternative (more robust) fix**: Remove the batch from inflight BEFORE deallocating, and add a guard check in `sendProduceRequests()`:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -869,6 +869,12 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n         ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection tpd = new ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection();\n         for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n             TopicPartition tp = batch.topicPartition;\n+\n+            // Skip batches that have already been deallocated (expired before sending)\n+            if (batch.isDone() && batch.finalState() == ProducerBatch.FinalState.FAILED) {\n+                continue;\n+            }\n+\n             MemoryRecords records = batch.records();\n             Uuid topicId = topicIds.get(tp.topic());\n             ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceData tpData = tpd.find(tp.topic(), topicId);\n```\n\nThe **first fix is preferred** because it's simpler and prevents the batch from ever being sent if it's already failed.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Producer sends messages to topic A** at various times with `linger.ms` configured\n2. **Batch waits in accumulator** for either batch size threshold or linger time\n3. **Batch becomes ready and is drained** from accumulator into `batches` map in `sendProducerData()` at line 395\n4. **Batch is added to inFlightBatches** at line 396, marking it as \"in flight\"\n5. **Expiration check runs** at line 406, iterating through inFlightBatches\n6. **Batch is found expired** because `createdMs` is old (timestamp from initial creation) but `now` has exceeded `delivery.timeout.ms`\n7. **Batch is removed from inFlightBatches** during iteration at line 191 in `getExpiredInflightBatches()`\n8. **failBatch() is called** at line 418, which calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `accumulator.deallocate()`\n9. **Buffer is released to BufferPool** and immediately becomes available for reuse\n10. **New batch for topic B** (from another thread or subsequent sends) allocates the reused buffer\n11. **sendProduceRequests() is still called** at line 442 with the original `batches` map containing the now-deallocated batch\n12. **batch.records() creates MemoryRecords** wrapping the deallocated buffer at line 874\n13. **Request is built with corrupted MemoryRecords** and queued for sending\n14. **Network layer serializes request** by calling `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` which reads from the reused buffer\n15. **Buffer now contains topic B's data**, so serialization includes wrong topic information\n16. **Broker receives request** with topic A's partition but topic B's data\n17. **Messages appear on topic B** while being sent to topic A's partition\n\n### Why This Is a Race Condition\n\nThe race condition is NOT between multiple threads (the Sender is single-threaded), but rather a **timing race between expiration checking and request sending within the same single-threaded method**.\n\nThe vulnerability exists because:\n- No check prevents a batch from being both drained AND expired in the same `sendProducerData()` call\n- No synchronization between deallocating a batch and sending its buffered request\n- The `batches` map is not cleared of deallocated batches before `sendProduceRequests()` is called\n- MemoryRecords holds a direct reference to the ByteBuffer without copying data\n\n### When This Manifests\n\n- When `delivery.timeout.ms` is relatively small\n- When `linger.ms` is large, causing batches to accumulate and age\n- During broker restarts/network disruptions (metrics show \"bursts\")\n- With high throughput where buffers are quickly reused\n- Most likely to occur when a batch is drained after being dequeued and retried multiple times\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":76,"oldLines":7,"newStart":76,"newLines":7,"lines":[" "," ## Proposed Fix"," ","-The fix is to **prevent deallocating a batch before its request is sent**, or Here are the key findings:\n\n### **Root Cause**\nIn `Sender.sendProducerData()` (lines 395-442), a batch can be **drained, added to inflight, and then immediately expired** within the same method call:\n\n1. **Line 395-396**: Batch is drained from accumulator and added to `inFlightBatches`\n2. **Line 406-407**: `getExpiredInflightBatches()` iterates through the SAME `inFlightBatches` map and finds the just-added batch has exceeded `delivery.timeout.ms` (because its `createdMs` is old)\n3. **Line 418**: `failBatch()` deallocates the batch's ByteBuffer back to `BufferPool`, which is immediately reused\n4. **Line 442**: `sendProduceRequests()` still tries to send the deallocated batch\n\n### **Why Data Gets Corrupted**\n- The `MemoryRecords` object returned by `batch.records()` holds a direct reference to the ByteBuffer\n- When the network layer serializes the request via `MemoryRecords.writeTo()`, it reads directly from the reused buffer\n- If the buffer is now part of a different topic's batch, the produce request header gets corrupted\n- Messages sent to topic A appear on topic B\n\n### **The Fix**\nRemove expired batches from the send queue before deallocating them:\n\n```java\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    batches.values().forEach(list -> list.remove(expiredBatch));  // NEW\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false);\n}\n```\n\nCombined with a defensive guard in `sendProduceRequests()`:\n```java\nif (batch.isDone()) continue;  // Skip already-failed batches\n```\n\nThe complete analysis with code traces, file locations, and detailed explanations has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1776,"cache_read_input_tokens":76303,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1776},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4bb75ef4-45ce-4348-86cb-b5dfe5e32610","uuid":"c7d4eea3-bee6-40b5-abb7-e4956c298d06"}
